URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS731842817	2019-03-31 15:20:42	1253	species	Himalayan Snowcock	Tetraogallus himalayensis			3				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Elko	US-NV-007	US-NV_2219	9			Island Lake	L3008742	H	40.6153207	-115.3816366	2006-08-25	05:45:00	obsr965477	S54417404	Historical	P62	EBIRD	335			2	0		0	1	0			We arrived at the trailhead at 0430 hrs. and began hiking uphill to Island Lk. by flashlight.  --It took us approx. 1 hr., 15 mins. to reach the lake (0545 hrs.).  Then we climbed a couple --of hundred vertical feet above the lake cross-country.  The temp. at around dawn was 40 --degrees F.  ----I observed the first two birds walking among the vegetation at long distance --(with only 10x binos) at approx. 0710 hrs.  Three birds were later seen --hop-flying onto boulders; this showed off the large amount of white in their --wings.  They seemed to be the color of the rust-stained gray granite rocks.  --Later, as we sat near the upper limit of the alpine vegetation in the cirque --(perhaps 600 ft. or more above the lake), we heard bugling elk-like calls as --well as other odd sounds.  At approx. 0925 I saw one snowcock perched atop --the Thomas Peak summit at 11,318 ft., high above us.  A minute or two later --another appeared, and then three (probably the same three observed earlier) --suddenly launched themselves off the promontory (broad white bands in the --wings very visible), landing in the vegetation of the next cirque to the north!  --We saw them quite well in their rather spectacular flight but lost them upon --landing.----We found what we presumed to be snowcock droppings (photo) and small --pits in the earth where they might have dug tubers--there were many of these --in evidence.  ----The lake elev. is 9,676, and we had climbed up at least another 600 vertical --ft. over the talus and scree to about 10,500 ft.----We had lunch lakeside after the triumphant observations and left there at --1120 hrs., arriving back at our vehicle at 1220 hrs.  A great day!

Despite being an introduced bird, this was well worth it because of the setting and the fact that I've not seen snowcock anywhere before. At first I could not see any movement on the ridges above the lake at all but then I heard the birds calling and eventually spotted one, then two and three males. They picked their way along the skyline, one bird somewhat lower than the others, allowing OK views by scope and even some grainy photos. Sometimes the birds would pause and call. At that point I realized there was another individual on the other side calling also but I could not see it. This was definitely a two thumbs up experience!

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS333020017	2017-04-26 21:14:57	1253	species	Himalayan Snowcock	Tetraogallus himalayensis			8				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Elko	US-NV-007	US-NV_2219	9			Island Lake	L3008742	H	40.6153207	-115.3816366	2015-07-23	04:46:00	obsr131100	S24357937	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	181	1.207		1	1		0	1	0		Left Elko at 2:25 AM, reached parking a bit after 3:00 AM and was at the top of the Island Lake trail by 4:30, still dark and no bird activity. No other people up there, which was a nice bonus. Climbed higher and got into position as it became light enough to start scoping. Chill wind coming down off crest. Wasn't properly prepared: needed gloves and a third layer. Temp felt like low 40's. Seemed to drop once I was on top. Back down to Island Lake at 7:41. Still cold but some sunshine breaking through.	Conservative estimate. Birds started calling at 5:10 AM and were quite vocal until 6:00 AM. Mix of males making classic bugle calls and general squabbling (more chicken like) within groups. Three separate males calling, essentially from each of the main rock walls. Eventually spotted a party of 4 below the central wall and watched them for about 40 mins. Some digiscoped photos and video. At least 1 calling male well right of these and a group of birds (guessing at 3+ by the racket) to the left. Didn't see any birds fly this time. Between 6 and 7:00 there was intermittent calling but subdued. Fantastic birds in a superb location.

Temperatures from 60 to 77. Birded with Brad Davis, who added Himalayan Snowcock to his life list...third time was the charm.	We heard a few Himalayan Snowcocks calling from the higher altitudes as we arrived at Island Lake at about 7:00 am. We first found one in a scope view at about 8:30 am. Two were seen, but a few others were heard also. The two that were seen were found feeding in one of the highest, grassy, vegetated areas in the middle of the bowl area, which was viewed from the area about a tenth of a mile above Island Lake. Later they hopped up on the rocks just above that vegetated area and preened, and were there until we headed back down the trail at about 10:40 am.

From Island Lake go right skirting the lake. Then maybe 2/3 around toward top of lake, climb the hill to first knoll (200-300 yards). No trail at this point but good walking. At top of knoll go lift up rise until you can see entire canyon and Wetland down below. Multiple birds calling when I arrived at 5:45 (rally call and display call as well as another almost whimpering melodic call given by pair). Really hard to see on ground. 3 flybys   Seem to be paired and displaying. Would climb up cliff a ways and then the pair would launch, gliding across the canyon calling to each other. Left then still calling and displaying at 9am. But get there at dawn for the best show. It took me 1-1/2 hrs to hike the 2+ mikes from the parking lot.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS933584340	2020-06-03 13:29:42	1253	species	Himalayan Snowcock	Tetraogallus himalayensis			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Elko	US-NV-007	US-NV_2219	9			Island Lake	L3008742	H	40.6153207	-115.3816366	2020-05-25	06:35:00	obsr44754	S69770994	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	335	32.171		1	1		0	1	0		This checklist covers the Lamoille Canyon drive, the hike to the Island Lake and the lake itself.	First stopped at the Lamoille Glacier Overlook at 6:30 AM to scan, listen and play the call. Did that systematically all the way along the canyon to the end of the road but no birds heard or seen. I hiked to Island Lake from 7:15 to 8:45 AM, playing the call along the way. No response along the way or at the lake, initially. I switched from playing the Kazakhstan recording to the Ruby Mts recording:--http://www.backpackingintherubymountains.info/himalayan/snowcockcall1.mp3  Within a minute, one responded from the hills west of the lake and couple minutes later, just before 9 AM, a snowcock came flying in. Watched it with bins as it disappeared behind the hill north. I climbed the hill, played the call and scanned the black hills & Thomas Peak for 45 minutes but no more response. The lake was frozen & without water birds. No people on the trail or at the lake until ~9:30 AM. It was light by 5 AM. Hiking quickly you can get to the lake in ~1 hour. I came down in 30 minutes. You can camp at Island Lake w/o permit or Thomas Canyon Campground 3 miles down the road. Reserve at https://www.recreation.gov/camping/campgrounds/232112?q=Thomas%20Canyon

This was a serious hike to find the Himalayan Snowcock. we started hiking at 4:30 and got to Island Lake around 5:20am. From there I scoped out a location that was Northwest of the lake and we started our accent. We got to about 10,000 when we were blessed to find a group of Snowcocks glide in about a thousand feet about us. I got my scope out again and ID'd them. At first we could only see four then as we looked closer we found a total of 9. It was breathtaking. We sent the next hour carefully making our way up scree rock and trying to get closer. We got about 500 feet below the ridge but they had disappeared by then. They are like ghosts. In a few shots they really seem to have disappeared to reappear in a completely  different place.
